Gene id and group are found in Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#MOESM12">7g</a></p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2/figures/4" data-track-dest="link:Figure4 Full size image" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#global-icon-chevron-right"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec10">Alignment of markers from an F2 mapping population to <i>V. riparia</i> and <i>V. vinifera</i> genome assemblies implies translocation events</h3><p>SNP marker sequences for F2 mapping population derived from a single F1 (generated by crossing <i>V. riparia</i> ‘Manitoba 37’ (female; grandmother) and the cultivar ‘Seyval’ (male; grandfather)) previously identified from GBS SNP analysis against <i>V. vinifera</i> PN40024 12X.1 genome were used to evaluate the utility of the <i>V. riparia</i> genome as a reference. Alignment of the SNP marker sequence to <i>V. riparia</i> ‘Manitoba 37’ and <i>V. vinifera</i> ‘PN40024’ chromosomes indicated that 89.5% of the markers aligned to both species, while about 6.2% and 4.2% mapped uniquely to <i>V. riparia</i> or <i>V. vinifera</i>, respectively (Supplementary Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#MOESM5">5a, b</a>, Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#MOESM13">8</a>). The number of markers that mapped was not proportional to genome or chromosome size between the two species indicating an even distribution (Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#MOESM13">8</a>). Putative rearrangements, needing further study to verify, were noted on sections of chromosomes 5, 6, and 8 appear between the two species, as well as between chromosomes 14 and 15 (Supplementary Fig. 6b).</p><p>Using the aligned SNP markers and phenotype data for flower sex and summer lateral shoot cessation photoperiod response, we identified and aligned genes between flanking markers of the respective QTL (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#Fig5">5a, b</a>) in the <i>V. riparia</i> pseudo-chromosomes and the <i>V. vinifera</i> ‘PN40024’ chromosomes. Genes in common between the species with similar position alignment and markers with similar LOD score as well as differential marker LOD and gene distribution differences are apparent.</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-5" data-title="Genome browser view of genes contained within F2-derived QTL regions represented in V. riparia and V. vinifera ’PN40024’ genomes that are aligned by the GBS markers."><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig5" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Fig. 5: Genome browser view of genes contained within F2-derived QTL regions represented in <i>V. riparia</i> and <i>V. vinifera</i> ’PN40024’ genomes that are aligned by the GBS markers.</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2/figures/5" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41438-020-0316-2/MediaObjects/41438_2020_316_Fig5_HTML.png?as=webp"></source><img aria-describedby="figure-5-desc" src="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41438-020-0316-2/MediaObjects/41438_2020_316_Fig5_HTML.png" alt="figure5" loading="lazy" width="685" height="329" /></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-5-desc"><p>The QTL’s represented are for <b>a</b> summer lateral critical photoperiod growth cessation and <b>b</b> flower type. In the top–middle row, markers found within a genomic region of each genome between the two flanking markers are plotted by their relative position along the <i>x</i> axis and the LOD score along the <i>y</i> axis. The LOD score at each marker is normalized and represented as values between 0 and 1 of the maximum LOD score. F2 markers present in <i>V. riparia</i> are colored red and those present in <i>V. vinifera</i> are blue. In the two bottom panels, genes are annotated by PFAM name, and genes within the QTL in both genomes are colored orange. In the top row, marker positions within the F2 genetic map are connected to the same marker position on each genome. Gene id and PFAM names are found in Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#MOESM14">9</a></p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2/figures/5" data-track-dest="link:Figure5 Full size image" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#global-icon-chevron-right"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="Sec11" data-title="Discussion"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec11-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec11">Discussion</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec11-content"><p>The first published <i>Vitis</i> reference genome for cultivated grapevine was produced using a highly homozygous inbred line derived from <i>V. vinifera</i> ‘Pinot noir’<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 23" title="Jaillon, O. et al. The grapevine genome sequence suggests ancestral hexaploidization in major angiosperm phyla. Nature 449, 463–467 (2007)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR23" id="ref-link-section-d4420e1694">23</a></sup>. While immensely useful in early genomic studies in grape, this inbred individual does not reflect the high heterozygosity found in other grapevine species and cultivars. The principal component analysis showed that <i>V. riparia</i> ‘Manitoba 37’ is likely a good representative reference for the <i>V. riparia</i> genome as it clusters with most of the collected diversity of this species. Both <i>V. riparia</i> ‘Manitoba 37’ and the other sequenced <i>V. riparia</i> genome ‘Gloire de Montpellier’<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 24" title="Girollet, N. et al. De novo phased assembly of Vitis riparia grape genome. Sci. Data 6, 127 (2019)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR24" id="ref-link-section-d4420e1711">24</a></sup> are part of this core diversity. When examined at other principal component levels, ‘Manitoba 37’ appears to be more genetically related to Midwest and Eastern collections of <i>V. riparia</i> than the <i>V. riparia ‘</i>Gloire de Montpellier’. Unfortunately, geographic passport data for the ‘Gloire’ variety is unknown and its representation of <i>V. riparia</i> may not be verifiable. The analysis presented here using only <i>V. riparia</i> data also suggests, for the first time, that there may be two clades of <i>V. riparia</i>, with the North Dakota and Montana genotypes forming the second subclade of genotypes. This result was not observed when examining GBS based relationship data as presented by Klein et al<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 10" title="Klein, L. L. et al. High-throughput sequencing data clarify evolutionary relationships among North American Vitis species and improve identification in USDA Vitis germplasm collection. Am. J. Bot. 105, 215–216 (2018)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR10" id="ref-link-section-d4420e1731">10</a></sup>, presumably due to the inclusion of a much wider collection of SNP data across the <i>Vitis</i> genus in that study. Our results demonstrate the potential for cryptic speciation within <i>V. riparia</i> for this Northwestern subclade of genotypes, or loss of diversity due to population extinction or poor representation in the USDA germplasm collection for the full diversity of the species.</p><p>Recently, an improved reference genome <i>V. vinifera</i> ‘PN40024’ was published with improved gene prediction and annotation<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 25" title="Canaguier, A. et al. A new version of the grapevine reference genome assembly (12X.v2) and of its annotation (VCost.v3). Genomics Data 14, 56–62 (2017)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR25" id="ref-link-section-d4420e1747">25</a></sup>. Genomes for other <i>V. vinifera</i> cultivars, as well as the rootstock variety ‘Riparia Gloire de Montpellier’ have recently been produced as well<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 24" title="Girollet, N. et al. De novo phased assembly of Vitis riparia grape genome. Sci. Data 6, 127 (2019)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR24" id="ref-link-section-d4420e1754">24</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Chin, C.-S. et al. Phased diploid genome assembly with single-molecule real-time sequencing. Nat. Methods 13, 1050–1054 (2016)." href="#ref-CR26" id="ref-link-section-d4420e1757">26</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Minio, A. et al. Diploid genome assembly of the wine grape Carménère. G3 9, 1331–1337 (2019)." href="#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d4420e1757_1">27</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 28" title="Roach, M. J. et al. Population sequencing reveals clonal diversity and ancestral inbreeding in the grapevine cultivar Chardonnay. PLoS Genet. 14, e1007807 (2018)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR28" id="ref-link-section-d4420e1760">28</a></sup>. However, there remains a dearth of genome data available for wild grapevine species, and those being used in breeding programs in particular. Illumina short-read are very accurate and preserve the heterozygosity of the genome sequence; however, they provide a more fractured assembly than long-read sequences. For example, the <i>V. vinifera</i> ‘Sultanina’ genome, Illumina sequences were used to construct a haploidified assembly<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 29" title="Di Genova, A. et al. Whole genome comparison between table and wine grapes reveals a comprehensive catalog of structural variants. BMC Plant Biol. 14, 7 (2014)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR29" id="ref-link-section-d4420e1768">29</a></sup> and subsequently an improved assembly with higher fidelity to the genotypes heterozygous nature was developed using the PLATANUS short-read assembler<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 30" title="Patel, S. et al. Comparison of three assembly strategies for a heterozygous seedless grapevine genome assembly. BMC Genomics 19, 57 (2018)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR30" id="ref-link-section-d4420e1772">30</a></sup>. With interest in developing an assembly that could be used for the development of molecular markers for <i>V. riparia</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 3" title="Zou, C. et al. Haplotyping the Vitis collinear core genome with rhAmpSeq improves marker transferability in a diverse genus. Nat. Commun. 11, 413 (2020)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR3" id="ref-link-section-d4420e1778">3</a></sup> Illumina short-read paired-end sequencing and mate paired long insert libraries were employed in the present study to assemble the heterozygous, diploid <i>V. riparia</i> ‘Manitoba 37’ genome.</p><p>This draft genome sequence, assembled using high quality Illumina reads (&gt;369X coverage), provides a valuable resource for marker development and breeding efforts using wild germplasm. The assembly of 495 Mb in 69,616 scaffolds, has an N50 of 518 kb which is greater than the N50 value reported for the <i>V. vinifera</i> ‘Sultanina’ genome assembled using Illumina data<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 30" title="Patel, S. et al. Comparison of three assembly strategies for a heterozygous seedless grapevine genome assembly. BMC Genomics 19, 57 (2018)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR30" id="ref-link-section-d4420e1791">30</a></sup>. The closest <i>Vitis</i> representative to our draft genome is <i>V. riparia</i> ‘Riparia Gloire de Montpellier’, a widely used rootstock variety. Interestingly, the long-read genome assembly of the ‘Gloire’ variety reports 33.9% repetitive sequences, far less than the 46% repeat sequences we detected in ‘Manitoba 37’ (which is similar <i>V. vinifera</i> ‘PN40024’ (41.4%))<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 24" title="Girollet, N. et al. De novo phased assembly of Vitis riparia grape genome. Sci. Data 6, 127 (2019)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR24" id="ref-link-section-d4420e1805">24</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 25" title="Canaguier, A. et al. A new version of the grapevine reference genome assembly (12X.v2) and of its annotation (VCost.v3). Genomics Data 14, 56–62 (2017)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR25" id="ref-link-section-d4420e1808">25</a></sup>. Several <i>Vitis</i> genome assemblies have been developed recently using Illumina HiSeq, PacBio RSII or 10X Chromium Genomics<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 24" title="Girollet, N. et al. De novo phased assembly of Vitis riparia grape genome. Sci. Data 6, 127 (2019)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR24" id="ref-link-section-d4420e1815">24</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Chin, C.-S. et al. Phased diploid genome assembly with single-molecule real-time sequencing. Nat. Methods 13, 1050–1054 (2016)." href="#ref-CR26" id="ref-link-section-d4420e1818">26</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Minio, A. et al. Diploid genome assembly of the wine grape Carménère. G3 9, 1331–1337 (2019)." href="#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d4420e1818_1">27</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 28" title="Roach, M. J. et al. Population sequencing reveals clonal diversity and ancestral inbreeding in the grapevine cultivar Chardonnay. PLoS Genet. 14, e1007807 (2018)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR28" id="ref-link-section-d4420e1821">28</a></sup>. The alignment results of <i>V. riparia</i> ‘Manitoba 37’ with primary contigs of <i>V. vinifera</i> cultivars was greater than 74% and as expected, the greatest alignment occurred with <i>V. riparia</i> ‘Riparia Gloire de Montpellier’ PACBio assembly<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 24" title="Girollet, N. et al. De novo phased assembly of Vitis riparia grape genome. Sci. Data 6, 127 (2019)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR24" id="ref-link-section-d4420e1835">24</a></sup>. Further evidence of quality can be seen in the similarity of <i>V. riparia</i> and <i>V. vinifera</i> genes identified in a common orthologous core across multiple genus, which indicate not only gene preservation across genetic distance, but provide evidence of assembly quality. In addition, assembly quality was indicated by the strong relationship found between the predicted <i>V. riparia</i> and <i>V. vinifera</i> genes. Indeed, the strong similarity of <i>LBD</i> and <i>WRKY</i> transcription factor families, between <i>V. riparia</i> and <i>V. vinifera</i> provide further evidence of assembly quality<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 31" title="Grimplet, J., Pimentel, D., Agudelo-Romero, P., Martinez-Zapater, J. M. &amp; Fortes, A. M. The lateral organ boundaries domain gene family in grapevine: genome-wide characterization and expresson analyses during developmental processes and stress responses. Sci. Rep. 7, 15968 (2017)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR31" id="ref-link-section-d4420e1864">31</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 32" title="Wang, M. et al. Genome and transcriptome analysis of the grapevine (Vitis vinifera L.) WRKY gene family. Hortic. Res. 1, 14016 (2014)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR32" id="ref-link-section-d4420e1867">32</a></sup>. The validation, completeness and accuracy of <i>V. riparia</i> ‘Manitoba 37’ genome features indicate that using only short-read Illumina sequences a high quality <i>V. riparia</i> genome assembly was developed.</p><p><i>V. riparia</i> is typically used in breeding programs to incorporate abiotic stress tolerance traits into new hybrid cultivars. Thus, particular attention was paid to examining the <i>WRKY</i>, <i>MYB</i>, and <i>ERF</i> transcription factors that influence gene regulation and have a strong role in abiotic stress tolerance phenotypes<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Wang, M. et al. Genome and transcriptome analysis of the grapevine (Vitis vinifera L.) WRKY gene family. Hortic. Res. 1, 14016 (2014)." href="#ref-CR32" id="ref-link-section-d4420e1891">32</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Eulgem, T., Rushton, P. J., Robatzek, S. &amp; Somssich, I. E. The WRKY superfamily of plant transcription factors. Trends Plant Sci. 5, 199–206 (2000)." href="#ref-CR33" id="ref-link-section-d4420e1891_1">33</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 34" title="Licausi, F. et al. Genomic and transcriptomic analysis of the AP2/ERF superfamily in Vitis vinifera. BMC Genomics 11, 719 (2010)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR34" id="ref-link-section-d4420e1894">34</a></sup>. The <i>V. riparia</i> predicted <i>WRKY</i> coding sequences were consistent with the published <i>V. vinifera</i> ‘PN40024’ 12X.1 <i>WRKY</i> groups<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 32" title="Wang, M. et al. Genome and transcriptome analysis of the grapevine (Vitis vinifera L.) WRKY gene family. Hortic. Res. 1, 14016 (2014)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR32" id="ref-link-section-d4420e1911">32</a></sup> and the V3 annotation of 12X.2<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 25" title="Canaguier, A. et al. A new version of the grapevine reference genome assembly (12X.v2) and of its annotation (VCost.v3). Genomics Data 14, 56–62 (2017)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR25" id="ref-link-section-d4420e1915">25</a></sup>, showing a great level of conservation between the species. The <i>MYB</i> family of transcription factor genes was explored specifically because of their importance to color, flavor and chemistry in grapevine species. Phylogenetic reconstruction of <i>MYB</i> subgroups found that the subgroups (4, 13, and 24) that had potential paralogous duplications were involved in ABA response, flavanol synthesis, secondary growth and anther development<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 35" title="Jin, J. et al. PlantTFDB 4.0: toward a central hub for transcription factors and regulatory interactions in plants. Nucleic Acids Res. 45, D1040–D1045 (2017)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR35" id="ref-link-section-d4420e1926">35</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 36" title="Gonzalez, A., Zhao, M., Leavitt, J. M. &amp; Loyd, A. M. Regulation of the anthocyanin pathway by the TTG1/bHLH/Myb transcriptional complex in Arabidopsis seedlings. Plant J. 53, 814–827 (2008)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR36" id="ref-link-section-d4420e1929">36</a></sup>. The only homologues with deletions in <i>V. riparia</i> ‘Manitoba 37’ was <i>MYB</i>113 of subgroup 6 which has been shown to regulate the production of anthocyanins in a <i>BASIS HELIX-LOOP-HELEX</i> (<i>bHLH</i>) dependent manner<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 36" title="Gonzalez, A., Zhao, M., Leavitt, J. M. &amp; Loyd, A. M. Regulation of the anthocyanin pathway by the TTG1/bHLH/Myb transcriptional complex in Arabidopsis seedlings. Plant J. 53, 814–827 (2008)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR36" id="ref-link-section-d4420e1946">36</a></sup>. We also noted an increased number of <i>bHLH</i> genes predicted in <i>V. riparia</i> ‘Manitoba 37’ genome assembly (by &gt; 20 genes) which is known to produce high amounts of predominantly diglucoside derivatives as opposed to monoglucosides in <i>V. vinifera</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 37" title="Li, Z., Pan, Q., Jin, Z., Mu, L. &amp; Duan, C. Comparison on phenoloic compounds in Vitis vinifera cv. Cabernet Sauvignon wines from five wine-growing regions in China. Food Chem. 125, 77–83 (2011)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR37" id="ref-link-section-d4420e1958">37</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 38" title="Liang, Z. et al. Anthocyanin composition and content in grape berry skin in Vitis germplasm. Food Chem. 111, 837–844 (2008)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR38" id="ref-link-section-d4420e1961">38</a></sup>. This result adds genomic context to one of the key issues facing acceptance of hybrid derived grape products as the presence of diglucoside derivatives is considered an indication of low quality in hybrid wines<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 39" title="Manns, D. C., Lenerz, C. T. M. C. &amp; Mansfield, A. K. Impact of processing parameters on the phenolic profile of wines produced from hybrid red grapes Maréchal Foch, Corot noir, and Marquette. J. Food Sci. 78, 696–702 (2013)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR39" id="ref-link-section-d4420e1965">39</a></sup>. Analysis of <i>ERF</i> genes using alignment and motif comparison between <i>V. riparia</i> and <i>V. vinifera</i> found functional similarities between members of each subfamily from both genomes. However, there were many instances of duplications present in <i>V. vinifera</i> ‘PN40024’ that were not present in our assembly, such as in subfamily IX where some duplications presented with different motifs.</p><p>Retrotransposon activity has long been associated with diversification of species clades. We observed a lower number of genes associated with transposases and retrotransposons in the <i>V. riparia</i> ‘Manitoba 37’ and <i>V. vinifera ‘</i>Sultanina’ than in the <i>V. vinifera</i> 12X.2. All three species seemed to share common ancestors for each LTR gene but experienced paralogous gene duplication at different rates in each clade. We posit that this change in retrotransposons could have played some impact on the divergent evolution of the species, as it has been found previously that Tvv1 transposon markers could accurately distinguish between North American species and <i>V. vinifera</i> cultivars<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 40" title="Sant’Ana, G. C. et al. Comparison of a retrotransposon-based marker with microsatellite markers for discriminating accessions of Vitis vinifera. Genet. Mol. Res. 11, 1507–1525 (2012)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR40" id="ref-link-section-d4420e1998">40</a></sup>.</p><p>The SNP markers that were developed using GBS of the F2 population in comparison with <i>V. vinifera ‘</i>PN40024’ 12X.1 allowed further analysis of the <i>V. riparia</i> ‘Manitoba 37’ assembly. Aligning these SNP markers with the pseudochromosomes of the grandparent, <i>V. riparia</i> ‘Manitoba 37’ and the <i>V. vinifera</i> ‘PN40024’ 12X.2 chromosomes showed that the F2 population more closely modeled <i>V. riparia</i> ‘Manitoba 37’. This can be expected since informative SNPs were predicted using the F2 grandparents and the male parent ‘Seyval’ has a complex pedigree including <i>V. vinifera</i> and other species. The presence of markers that aligned to chromosome 20 of <i>V. vinifera</i>, un-assembled scaffolds, but to other chromosomes on <i>V. riparia</i> may give us a better indication of the actual genomic position of those scaffolds on <i>V. vinifera ‘</i>PN40024’ assembly. By using the markers that mapped to different chromosomes in female grandparent and <i>V. vinifera</i> as a representative portion of the male grandparent, we found evidence for potential large genomic alterations between these species that may have occurred during the evolution and geographic isolation 3.5–9.5 million years ago. When we look at areas of both genomes containing QTL’s we can see that large translocations between chromosomes shows missing genes found between flanking markers in <i>V. riparia</i> relative to <i>V. vinifera</i>, thus impacting the resulting observed phenotype. This shows the potential power of sequencing and assembling a genetic grandparent of a F2 population in identifying the genetic basis of QTL regions.</p><p>In conclusion, we present high coverage short-read draft genome sequence of the wild grapevine species <i>V. riparia</i>. This genome represents the second genome assembly of this critically important species and the first representative of a locally adapted stress tolerant genotype. The <i>V. riparia</i> ‘Manitoba 37’ genome assembly provides an important resource for comparative genomic and genetic marker studies. This <i>V. riparia</i> ‘Manitoba 37’ genome has already proven useful for the development of molecular markers in North American breeding programs and will serve as an important tool in the development of genomics-assisted selection for grapevine improvement, particularly for traits associated with abiotic and biotic stress resistance.</p></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="Sec12" data-title="Materials and methods"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec12-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec12">Materials and methods</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec12-content"><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec13"><i>V. riparia</i> ‘Manitoba 37’ materials</h3><p><i>V. riparia</i> ‘Manitoba 37’ (identified as ‘PI588259’ in USDA Germplasm Repository, Geneva, NY, USA) was used for sequencing. The genetic relationship of <i>V. riparia</i> ‘Manitoba 37’ to other <i>V. riparia</i> genotypes was analyzed using a data set extracted from genotype data collected from multiple species housed at the Geneva USDA-ARS grape germplasm repository<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 10" title="Klein, L. L. et al. High-throughput sequencing data clarify evolutionary relationships among North American Vitis species and improve identification in USDA Vitis germplasm collection. Am. J. Bot. 105, 215–216 (2018)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR10" id="ref-link-section-d4420e2078">10</a></sup>. To identify highly specific SNPs, VCFtools filters were applied to 156,799 SNPs from 74 unique <i>V. riparia</i> genotypes, keeping those found in at least 50% of the individuals, resulting in 54,029 SNPs<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 41" title="Danecek, P. et al. The variant call format and VCFtools. Bioinform 27, 2156–2158 (2011)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR41" id="ref-link-section-d4420e2085">41</a></sup>. We then removed six <i>V. riparia</i> genotypes with missing data at greater than 30% of the total SNPs. A high stringency filter was applied to the remaining SNPs keeping all SNPs found in 95% or greater of the <i>V. riparia</i> providing 1485 highly specific SNPs. SNPRelate R package<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 42" title="Zheng, X. et al. A high-performance computing toolset for relatedness and principal component analysis of SNP data. Bioinformatics 28, 3326–3328 (2012)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR42" id="ref-link-section-d4420e2096">42</a></sup> was used to calculate the principal components of the specific SNPs data set and plotted the 68 individuals using ggplot2<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 43" title="Wickham, H. ggplot2: Elegant Graphics for Data Analysis. (Springer-Verlag, New York, 2016)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR43" id="ref-link-section-d4420e2100">43</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec14">DNA sequencing and pre-processing of reads</h3><p>One centimeter diameter new leaves of greenhouse grown vines were used for DNA extraction and sequencing. A total of nine paired-end libraries were constructed with insert sizes of 346, 473, 478 by Illumina I and 250, 450, 600, 3–5 kb, 8–10 kb, 15–20 kb by Illumina Hiseq 2500 sequencer. In total, 2295.4 M raw reads were generated with 658.4X coverage and read length from 100 nt–260 nt (Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#MOESM15">10a</a>). Raw reads were then filtered and corrected using cutadapt, Trimmomatic, PEAR, FastUniq, Quake, and NGSTOOLKIT (Tool references are found in Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#MOESM15">10b</a>). The k-mer analysis was carried out with Jellyfish with 19 bp k-mers using only 262.3X coverage of filtered reads. The genome’s heterozygosity and other results were obtained with GenomeScope. All filtered reads used for de novo genome assembly were mapped back to our assembly using bowtie2. The SAM files of the bowtie2 mapping results were converted to BAM files using SAMtools, and then the alignment statistics were obtained using the flagstat option of SAMtools (Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#MOESM15">10b</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec15"><i>V. riparia</i> ‘Manitoba 37’ de novo heterozygous genome assembly and assembly evaluation</h3><p>A total of 1313.7 M filtered reads were used for de novo genome assembly. The first assembly was obtained with PLATANUS<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 44" title="Kajitani, R. et al. Efficient de novo assembly of highly heterozygous genomes from whole-genome shotgun short reads. Genome Res. 24, 1384–1395 (2014)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR44" id="ref-link-section-d4420e2132">44</a></sup> by changing parameters in each of the three steps ((assemble: -u 0.2 -d 0.3), (scaffold: -s 20 -v 20 -u 0.2) and (gap close: -s 20 -vo 20 -vd 20 -ed 0.1)).This assembly was processed with GapCloser and the result of this assembly was then subjected to a second round of GapCloser to produce the final assembly (<a href="https://openprairie.sdstate.edu/vitis_riparia_VR37_PI588259">https://openprairie.sdstate.edu/vitis_riparia_VR37_PI588259</a>) (All tool references are found in Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#MOESM15">10b</a>). The assembly was tested for contamination using DeconSeq. The assembly statistics were evaluated using an Assemblathon script and processed with reference genome <i>V. vinifera</i> ‘PN40024’ assembly<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 25" title="Canaguier, A. et al. A new version of the grapevine reference genome assembly (12X.v2) and of its annotation (VCost.v3). Genomics Data 14, 56–62 (2017)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR25" id="ref-link-section-d4420e2146">25</a></sup> 486,205,130 bp. The quality of the assembly was further assessed by four independent methods. (1) The percentage filtered reads were mapped back to the <i>V. riparia</i> ‘Manitoba 37’ genome using a zero mismatch. (2) The quality of the assembly was further assessed by using REAPR program which measures the number of times that there is low mapped mate-paired-end read coverage of any specific site to predict potential errors in contig assembly. While we found few mistakes in assembly of reads (only 16% of contigs had errors), we did observe low incidence of error free bases (maximum 42.11%). The reason for this low rate is unknown, however, REAPR is a relatively new tool in plant genome development and may not be properly calibrated for the high heterozygosity of this genome. (3) The <i>V. riparia</i> ‘Manitoba 37’ assembly quality was further characterized by generating a dot plot of <i>V. vinifera</i> ‘PN40024’ and <i>V. riparia</i> assembly using the D-genie program which plotted a sorted and denoised global alignment of the two assemblies. 4) <i>V. riparia</i> ESTs and BAC sequences and three de novo <i>V. riparia</i> transcriptomes were aligned with the genome. GMAP with default parameters was used to map and EST sequences of <i>V. riparia</i> from NCBI to our assembly (SAMN00174930, SAMN00152554, SAMN00152555, SAMN00152556, and SAMN00150676). Three <i>V. riparia</i> de novo transcriptomes (PI588259, PI588271, and PI588587), were aligned with the <i>V. riparia</i> genome assembly using BLAT. We used the MUMmer package for alignment of <i>V. riparia</i> BAC sequences (BioProject PRJNA550997) and <i>V. vinifera ‘</i>PN40024’<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 25" title="Canaguier, A. et al. A new version of the grapevine reference genome assembly (12X.v2) and of its annotation (VCost.v3). Genomics Data 14, 56–62 (2017)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR25" id="ref-link-section-d4420e2185">25</a></sup>. (1) BACs were aligned to each <i>V. riparia</i> scaffold using nucmer with -mum option. (2) The output results from nucmer were filtered using delta-filter with the -g option. (3) The filtered results were used in the show-coords program and the coordinates of the resulting alignments were obtained. (4) The alignments that represented the longest length (top-hit) for each BAC were summed (top-hits-length). The same steps were followed for mapping the de novo <i>V. riparia</i> ‘Manitoba 37’ assembly with the reference genome <i>V. vinifera</i> ‘PN40024’ (12X.2, V3), <i>V. vinifera</i> cv. Cabernet Sauvignon, <i>V. vinifera</i> ‘Chardonnay’, <i>V. vinifera</i> ‘Carménère’, and <i>V. riparia</i> ‘Riparia Gloire de Montpellier’.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec16"><i>V. riparia</i> SNP calling</h3><p>All filtered reads were aligned to the reference genome <i>V. vinifera</i> ‘PN40024’<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 25" title="Canaguier, A. et al. A new version of the grapevine reference genome assembly (12X.v2) and of its annotation (VCost.v3). Genomics Data 14, 56–62 (2017)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR25" id="ref-link-section-d4420e2226">25</a></sup> with bowtie2. The SAM files were converted to BAM files then repeats were removed by rmdup, followed by sorting in bowtie2. We called the SNPs using the mpileup of SAMtools with default parameters. Then, SNPs were filtered by VCFtools using a window of 10, a minimum depth of 8, and a minimum quality 40. SNP effect was predicted by using the SnpEff program (Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#MOESM15">10c</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec17">De novo gene prediction and functional annotation</h3><p>The repeats were identified with RepeatModeler and then repeats were masked by RepeatMasker (All tool references used in gene prediction and annotation are shown in Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#MOESM15">10d</a>). The RNAseq data of <i>V. riparia</i> from our lab were mapped to the masked <i>V. riparia</i> genome assembly and all.bam files were used for de novo gene prediction with BRAKER-1. The assembly gene coverage was preliminarily assessed by BUSCO (version 4.0.5), after gene prediction, using the latest plant early release database (embryophyta_odb10) in genome mode. Coding sequences were further annotated using Blast2GO. BLASTX was performed using the nr database with parameters of: E value 1.0E−3; number of blast hits 1, word size 6, HSP length cutoff 33, and eukaryotes selected as taxonomy. The results from the BLASTX of the assembly was then searched for enzyme classification databases: InterPro, GO (gene ontology), and KEGG pathway analysis using Blast2GO.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec18">Whole genome synteny analysis of <i>V. riparia</i> and <i>V. vinifera</i>
</h3><p>The de novo <i>V. riparia</i> assembly was aligned to reference genome <i>V. vinifera</i> ‘PN40024’<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 25" title="Canaguier, A. et al. A new version of the grapevine reference genome assembly (12X.v2) and of its annotation (VCost.v3). Genomics Data 14, 56–62 (2017)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR25" id="ref-link-section-d4420e2272">25</a></sup>. Masking of repeat sequences and gene predictions from this chromosome-level assembly were obtained as described above for the scaffold assembly. Syntenic blocks between the genomes of <i>V. riparia</i> and other <i>Vitis</i> genomes<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Girollet, N. et al. De novo phased assembly of Vitis riparia grape genome. Sci. Data 6, 127 (2019)." href="#ref-CR24" id="ref-link-section-d4420e2283">24</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Canaguier, A. et al. A new version of the grapevine reference genome assembly (12X.v2) and of its annotation (VCost.v3). Genomics Data 14, 56–62 (2017)." href="#ref-CR25" id="ref-link-section-d4420e2283_1">25</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Chin, C.-S. et al. Phased diploid genome assembly with single-molecule real-time sequencing. Nat. Methods 13, 1050–1054 (2016)." href="#ref-CR26" id="ref-link-section-d4420e2283_2">26</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Minio, A. et al. Diploid genome assembly of the wine grape Carménère. G3 9, 1331–1337 (2019)." href="#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d4420e2283_3">27</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 28" title="Roach, M. J. et al. Population sequencing reveals clonal diversity and ancestral inbreeding in the grapevine cultivar Chardonnay. PLoS Genet. 14, e1007807 (2018)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR28" id="ref-link-section-d4420e2286">28</a></sup> were computed by SyMAP (v4.2). <i>V. riparia</i> ‘Manitoba 37’ genome and gene models were aligned to all other genomes and gene models separately (<i>V. vinifera</i> ‘PN40024’<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 25" title="Canaguier, A. et al. A new version of the grapevine reference genome assembly (12X.v2) and of its annotation (VCost.v3). Genomics Data 14, 56–62 (2017)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR25" id="ref-link-section-d4420e2296">25</a></sup><i>, V. vinifera</i> ‘Sultanina’<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 30" title="Patel, S. et al. Comparison of three assembly strategies for a heterozygous seedless grapevine genome assembly. BMC Genomics 19, 57 (2018)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR30" id="ref-link-section-d4420e2302">30</a></sup><i>, Populus trichocarpa, Medicago truncatula</i>, and <i>Arabidopsis thaliana</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 45" title="Ensembl Plants. Available at: &#xA;http://plants.ensembl.org/index.html&#xA;&#xA;. (Accessed: 1st June 2019)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR45" id="ref-link-section-d4420e2311">45</a></sup>, and <i>Fragaria vesca</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 46" title="Sook Jung et al. 15 years of GDR: new data and functionality in the Genome Database for Rosaceae. Nucleic Acids Res. 47, D1137–D1145 (2018)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR46" id="ref-link-section-d4420e2317">46</a></sup>, using the promer option of the MUMmer program (Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#MOESM10">5b–d</a>). Syntenic blocks between <i>V. riparia</i> and all other genomes were obtained from a script in SyMAP (v4.2). (All tool references are in Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#MOESM15">10e</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec19">Analysis of orthologous genes</h3><p>All the predicted protein sequences from <i>V. riparia</i>, <i>V. vinifera</i> ‘PN40024’<i>, V. vinifera</i> Sultanina<i>, Populus, Fragaria</i>, and <i>Arabidopsis</i> were analyzed using OrthoMCL with default settings (All tool references are in Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#MOESM15">10e</a>). OrthoMCL was performed step-by-step as described in the manual. (1) An all vs. all BLASTP was performed to identify best hit pairs between species (orthologs), as well as sets of genes more closely related within than between species (in-paralogs). (2) This best hit matrix was used for ortholog definition with the parameter (<i>I</i>) = 1.5. 3). The results from OrthoMCL were visualized by OrthoVenn. The single copy gene present in all six species was used to generate a phylogenetic tree in the program MEGA7. (1) All protein sequences were aligned with ClustalW using PAM weight matrix. (2) The multiple sequence alignments were then used for phylogenetic tree construction by Maximum Likelihood method using default parameters in MEGA7.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec20">Plant transcription factors prediction and phylogenetic tree of gene families</h3><p>Using all predicted protein sequences from <i>V. riparia</i> ‘Manitoba 37’ assembly and <i>V. vinifera</i> ‘PN40024’ (12X.1, V2 and 12X.2, V3) annotation<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 25" title="Canaguier, A. et al. A new version of the grapevine reference genome assembly (12X.v2) and of its annotation (VCost.v3). Genomics Data 14, 56–62 (2017)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR25" id="ref-link-section-d4420e2374">25</a></sup> we predicted Plant transcription factors with PlantTFDB (4.0)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 35" title="Jin, J. et al. PlantTFDB 4.0: toward a central hub for transcription factors and regulatory interactions in plants. Nucleic Acids Res. 45, D1040–D1045 (2017)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR35" id="ref-link-section-d4420e2378">35</a></sup>. The <i>V. vinifera</i> ‘PN40024’ 12X.1, V2<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 47" title="Index of /DATA. (2016). Available at: &#xA;http://genomes.cribi.unipd.it/DATA&#xA;&#xA;/. (Accessed: 25th July 2019)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR47" id="ref-link-section-d4420e2386">47</a></sup> annotation was also used so that comparisons could be made with earlier transcription factor characterization publications. Transcription factors were predicted together for all assemblies so that comparisons could be made directly in this study. The <i>WRKY</i> gene family results and protein sequences of <i>V. riparia</i> ‘Manitoba 37’ and <i>V. vinifera</i> ‘PN40024’. 12X.1, V1; 12X.2, V3 were retrieved from PlantTFDB (4.0)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 35" title="Jin, J. et al. PlantTFDB 4.0: toward a central hub for transcription factors and regulatory interactions in plants. Nucleic Acids Res. 45, D1040–D1045 (2017)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR35" id="ref-link-section-d4420e2399">35</a></sup> and classified into different groups based on a previous <i>WRKY</i> study<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 32" title="Wang, M. et al. Genome and transcriptome analysis of the grapevine (Vitis vinifera L.) WRKY gene family. Hortic. Res. 1, 14016 (2014)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR32" id="ref-link-section-d4420e2407">32</a></sup>. We created a circular phylogenetic tree for <i>WRKY</i> in two steps, (1) <i>WRKY</i> protein sequences of <i>V. riparia</i> and <i>V. vinifera</i> ‘PN40024’ aligned together by ClustalW in MEGA7 (Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#MOESM15">10b</a>). The circular phylogenetic tree was then constructed by the neighbor-joining method using the complete deletion option and bootstrapping with 1000 replicates. Annotation of subgroups in <i>MYB</i> and <i>ERF</i> TFs was done through a BLAST alignment to classified <i>Arabidopsis</i> TFs in PlantTFDB<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 48" title="Dubos et al. MYB transcription factors in Arabidopsis. Trends Plant Sci. 15, 573–581 (2010)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR48" id="ref-link-section-d4420e2436">48</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 49" title="Nakano, T., Suzuki, K., Fujimura, T. &amp; Shinshi, H. Genome-wide analysis of the ERF gene family in Arabidopsis and Rice. Plant Physiol. 140, 411–432 (2006)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR49" id="ref-link-section-d4420e2439">49</a></sup>. The neighbor-joining tree for the <i>MYB</i> and <i>ERF</i> TFs was generated from a clustal alignment of all genes through R code ggtree and msa packages (Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#MOESM15">10f</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec21">Alignment of F2 GBS markers to <i>V. riparia</i> ‘Manitoba 37’ and <i>V. vinifera</i> ‘PN40024’ 12X.2</h3><p>The predicted <i>V. riparia</i> ‘Manitoba 37’ gene set and <i>V. vinifera</i> ‘PN40024’ annotation were aligned to the PFAM database using HMMer (All tool references for QTL alignment are in Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#MOESM15">10g</a>). The matching annotations were used to divide genes into families or domains. Then the differences in gene number for each gene family at each position of the corresponding gene on the <i>V. vinifera</i> chromosome were plotted with RCircos. The GBS genetic markers from a F2 mapping population, derived from a self of an individual F1 genotype from a cross of <i>V. riparia</i> ‘Manitoba 37’ and hybrid cultivar ‘Seyval’<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2" title="Yang et al. Next generation mapping of enological traits in an F2 interspecific grapevine hybrid family. PLoS ONE 11, e0149560 (2016)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR2" id="ref-link-section-d4420e2484">2</a></sup>, were then aligned to <i>V. vinifera</i> ‘PN40024’ 12X.2 and a pseudo-chromosomal assembly of <i>V. riparia</i> ‘Manitoba 37’. The <i>V. riparia</i> pseudo-chromosomal assembly was based on its genomic alignment to <i>V. vinifera</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 35" title="Jin, J. et al. PlantTFDB 4.0: toward a central hub for transcription factors and regulatory interactions in plants. Nucleic Acids Res. 45, D1040–D1045 (2017)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR35" id="ref-link-section-d4420e2499">35</a></sup>, using the Bowtie aligner (Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#MOESM15">10c</a>). R programming was used to find the common marker set and plot the markers mapping to chromosomes using RCircos (Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#MOESM15">10g</a>). The gene containing regions of <i>V. vinifera</i> 12X.2 and <i>V. riparia</i> ‘Manitoba 37’ were extracted from between QTL markers for previously predicted QTL flanking markers for female sex and summer lateral cessation in response to decreasing photoperiod phenotype on chromosome 2 and scaled to markers shared between the species<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2" title="Yang et al. Next generation mapping of enological traits in an F2 interspecific grapevine hybrid family. PLoS ONE 11, e0149560 (2016)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR2" id="ref-link-section-d4420e2516">2</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 18" title="Garris, A. et al. Mapping of photoperiod-induced growth cessation in the wild grape Vitis riparia. J. Am. Soc. Hort. Sci. 134, 261–272 (2009)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR18" id="ref-link-section-d4420e2519">18</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 19" title="Fennell, A., Alahakoon, D., Luby, J. &amp; Clark, M. Mapping the genetic architecture of grapevine bud growth-cycling quantitative traits. Acta Hort. 1248, 337–343 (2019)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0316-2#ref-CR19" id="ref-link-section-d4420e2522">19</a></sup>. The LOD score of the species-specific markers were then plotted using scaled LOD values to present species protein domain distribution.</p></div></div></section>
                

                <section aria-labelledby="data-availability" data-title="Data availability"><div class="c-article-section" id="data-availability-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="data-availability">Data availability</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="data-availability-content">
              
              <p>The raw reads of Illumina data and BAC sequences are found in the NCBI BioProject PRJNA550997. EST sequences were downloaded from existing NCBI nucleotide resources. The genome assembly, gene annotation, proteins, and other data are publically available at: <a href="https://openprairie.sdstate.edu/vitis_riparia_VR37_PI588259">https://openprairie.sdstate.edu/vitis_riparia_VR37_PI588259</a>.</p>
